The primary aim behind this innovation was to make poultry processing easier by eliminating the need for de-feathering, a step that consumes time and resources in traditional broiler farming.

This breed was also introduced as a way to improve heat tolerance in chickens, particularly in regions with hot climates. Feathers act as insulation, so in warmer environments, chickens can struggle with heat stress. Without feathers, featherless broilers can potentially stay cooler and thrive in hot conditions where conventional broilers might face difficulties.

However, the absence of feathers also creates challenges. Feathers serve as protection against environmental factors like cold weather, parasites, and injury. Without this natural barrier, featherless broilers are more vulnerable to these threats, requiring farmers to provide extra care, such as specialized housing and protection from injuries and cold temperatures.

Despite the potential benefits, the featherless broiler hasn’t been widely adopted, largely because of these vulnerabilities and concerns about the welfare of the birds. Managing their environment carefully is crucial to ensure they remain healthy and productive.

Would you stock featherless broilers?

✨The Lowdown✨

👉Best By or Enjoy by: This is just a suggestion for the day you should enjoy the product for peak flavor. It is NOT an expiration date!

👉Sell By: This date is for store displays and inventory. It is not a food safety guideline. Many foods are still good after this date.

👉Use By: This date is also a quality guideline, except when it comes to baby formula. For optimal nutrition, use baby formula by its use by date. Most other foods are still perfectly good past their use by date.

👉Freeze By: Freeze by this date to lock in freshness, but don’t panic if you miss it! It’s not a food safety date.
